<div id="review_2414341869" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2414341869" />
    <a title="Jen ♥Star-Crossed Book Blog♥" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/28353412-jen-star-crossed-book-blog"><img alt="Jen ♥Star-Crossed Book Blog♥" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1576986930p2/28353412.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2414341869?book_show_action=true">Feb 25, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jen ♥Star-Crossed Book Blog♥" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jen ♥Star-Crossed Book Blog♥" href="/user/show/28353412-jen-star-crossed-book-blog">Jen ♥Star-Crossed Book Blog♥</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781477817506" href="/book/show/18615935-beautifully-damaged">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28353412-jen-star-crossed-book-blog?shelf=kindle-unlimited">kindle-unlimited</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28353412-jen-star-crossed-book-blog?shelf=im-the-only-one-i-walk-alone">im-the-only-one-i-walk-alone</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2414341869" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4430378509492980354"><b>Beautifully Damaged pulled me in and then crashed and burned. </b>I haven't had a 1 star rating in almost 3 years, but there was no denying how I felt about this book. Even though this story held so much potential, the characters wore on me and I kept picking holes at the story. When I found myself skimming the last quarter of the book, I knew I was done. So my top three issues were...<br/><br/><b><strong>✩</strong>A doormat heroine</b><br/><blockquote>
  
    <b>He really was fucked up, but I loved him. I loved him enough to stay.</b>
  
</blockquote><br/>From the very fir</span>
  <span id="freeText4430378509492980354" style="display:none"><b>Beautifully Damaged pulled me in and then crashed and burned. </b>I haven't had a 1 star rating in almost 3 years, but there was no denying how I felt about this book. Even though this story held so much potential, the characters wore on me and I kept picking holes at the story. When I found myself skimming the last quarter of the book, I knew I was done. So my top three issues were...<br /><br /><b><strong>✩</strong>A doormat heroine</b><br /><blockquote>
  
    <b>He really was fucked up, but I loved him. I loved him enough to stay.</b>
  
</blockquote><br />From the very first chapter, we watched as Ember let her roommate walk all over her. Her roommate said rude things to her, took her stuff and even ditched her. All while Ember let her. And when she allowed Trace to do the same thing, I was done with her. I was so angry that she allowed herself to be a victim, again. It was frustrating that she never said anything when her boyfriend would be gone for all hours of the night or when she would catch him flirting with other girls. And there's a scene where it looks like he's having sex with another girl, ugh. Just no. <b>Her lack of actions made me completely lose any and all respect I had for her.</b> Yes she punched a guy in the beginning of the story and another person way down the road but it wasn't enough. Not near enough because of all of the other moments I painfully had to sit there and watch her do nothing.<br /><br /><b><strong>✩</strong>A jerk of a hero</b><br /><blockquote>
  
    <b>“You actually believe I could feel any other way about you? You are my forever.”<br /> “You’re not mine.”</b>
  
</blockquote><br />If you follow my reviews, you know I always love the guys that start off as a douche bag and then turn into so much more . But <b>with Trace Montgomery, I finally found a jerk I didn't like.</b> I tried my hardest to fall for him since he was thoughtful, caring and protective. But in the end, I just hated him. My first clue that I should have given up on him was when he was staring at Ember, while getting another girl off. My second clue should have been when he purposely flirted with other girls when Ember was around. My third clue should have been when he didn't care that he was tearing Ember apart when he threatened to bring another girl back to where they both lived. Ohhhh and he proceeded to warn Ember that the girl he was bringing back was a screamer. What a great guy *rolls eyes*. And while there was a ton more clues, the final nail in the coffin was when he made it look like he was fucking another girl while Ember walked in on it. Just NO. Trace pushed too hard. He pushed too far. I didn't care that his past made him the way he was. He was cold and callous in my eyes.<br /><br /><b><strong>✩</strong>WTFs</b><br /><blockquote>
  
    <b>I discovered that a body could still function when the heart was reduced to nothing but ash.</b>
  
</blockquote><br />I'm not even going to touch on the fact that we're told Ember is shy yet she has no problem singing in public or punching a guy in the face, or the cooking thing, or her tattoo she got before she even slept with Trace, or his stalking, because all of that was absolutely ridiculous. But <b>the huge revelation at the end? I'm sure that was supposed to make us happy, but all it did was make me livid. </b> The legal implications, the emotional scarring, the abandonment? Not to mention the complications in the future, I just, wow. Are you kidding me? It was messed up on so many levels and it left the worst taste in my mouth.<br /><br /><b>Beautifully Damaged was definitely not for me and I wont be picking up another book by this author. </b></span>
  <a data-text-id="4430378509492980354" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText5638772399055053304" style="display:none">Halfway through this book I need defibrillation--I've already been damaged and cannot make it till the end.<br /><br />But let me tell you this: Typically, I really appreciate the effort and focus of people who do everything they can to follow their dreams (people such as the author of this book). This is not the case, however, when it comes to killing people's brain cells with what is supposed to be literature, which also happens to be written in a way that makes English language run and scream for its life. <br /><br />I do feel the need to point at least two of the reasons behind my humble opinion of this read. <br /><br />1. Ember--Ember, oh dear Ember, what has life done to you? Were you buried in a cave? Under thick ice? On top of mount Everest? You are deluded and you make me feel funny (with all your stalking, blushing, tattooing-before-ever-had-sex-with-the-guy stuff...) and I don't think I could ever like you. EVER.<br /><br />2. And Trace--why, oh why did you let your balls get surgically removed? I thought you were supposed to be a bad boy, an alpha-male, and yet you somehow managed to turn into this annoying teenage girl blabbering about these demons...<br /><br />I kid you not, people, I can usually tolerate a lot of bull, but that book I could not stand and will not finish. Suffice to say that if it were up to me, I would never let this 'book' get published on paper...</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer2052708465354671978">L A Fiore has done something not many authors manage. She wrote a female character in a romance that I actually liked. Ember was smart, loving, independent and interesting.She also managed to write an extremely hot, but very damaged bad boy. I actually liked them both very much.   <span id="freeText2052708465354671978" style="display:none">L A Fiore has done something not many authors manage. She wrote a female character in a romance that I actually liked. Ember was smart, loving, independent and interesting.She also managed to write an extremely hot, but very damaged bad boy. I actually liked them both very much. Added to that a great cast of secondary characters, and I was already well on the way to liking this book.<br /><br />The storyline was really good. A romance that the hero could heal and grow from, while the heroine could have all her dreams come true. Liking this more.<br /><br />That was enough to have me liking this book. L A Fiore didn't stop there though. Oh no! I also got a pretty good mystery/stalker story as well. I ended up staying awake way past my bedtime so I could finish this. With all these things I liked about this book it ended up with me loving it.</span>

<div id="review_548111256" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/548111256" />
    <a title="Jenn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3349239-jenn"><img alt="Jenn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1397155775p2/3349239.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/548111256?book_show_action=true">Feb 27, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jenn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jenn" href="/user/show/3349239-jenn">Jenn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">BR w/ Jennifer &amp; Lindsay</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3349239-jenn?shelf=accident-coping-death-illness-grief">accident-coping-death-illness-grief</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3349239-jenn?shelf=abuse-neglect-serious-content">abuse-neglect-serious-content</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3349239-jenn?shelf=fighters-gaming-sports">fighters-gaming-sports</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3349239-jenn?shelf=twisty-plots">twisty-plots</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer548111256" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16077583292968981714"><b> Warning: </b><br/>This book may not be suitable for those who don't like: Eggs. Bacon. Or... Cake-pops.<br/>-It may cause hallucinations and or dreams about cake-pops. <br/>-You may go through withdrawals if you aren't stocked up on eggs, bacon or cake-pops.<br/><br/>Just a little taste of Ember's mind and cake pops:<br/><b>
  <i>"I was like a junkie and Trace was my drug. I had no will power when it came to him. He was like my life-size cake-pop..."</i>
</b><br/><br/><b> You have been warned.</b><br/><br/><i>
  <b>Holy Twists Batman! </b>
</i> The second half of this book is full </span>
  <span id="freeText16077583292968981714" style="display:none"><b> Warning: </b><br />This book may not be suitable for those who don't like: Eggs. Bacon. Or... Cake-pops.<br />-It may cause hallucinations and or dreams about cake-pops. <br />-You may go through withdrawals if you aren't stocked up on eggs, bacon or cake-pops.<br /><br />Just a little taste of Ember's mind and cake pops:<br /><b>
  <i>"I was like a junkie and Trace was my drug. I had no will power when it came to him. He was like my life-size cake-pop..."</i>
</b><br /><br /><b> You have been warned.</b><br /><br /><i>
  <b>Holy Twists Batman! </b>
</i> The second half of this book is full of twists and turns. However, I should probably start at the beginning. <br /><br />The first half of the book is focused on Ember and Trace's friendship and relationship. It brings in to play a few bad characters and Embers friend/roommate Lena. As well as her good friend Trent. Trace and Ember work out a friendship that eventually turns in to a dating relationship. Trace has demons from his past that effect how he deals with life and sometimes Ember. Also, in the first half, we meet some awesome friends and family members who are great secondary characters. <br /><br />The second half the book has some twists and turns and a little suspense of "Who did it" mixed in. It also has a very nice balance of Trace and Ember's relationship mixed in as well. <br /><br />I loved how Trace and Ember start their relationship. They build up a friendship and hang out. Even though there's an instant and deep attraction to one another, these two play the friendship card first and never rush anything. Even after they start dating they never rush the intimacy. These two were perfect for each other. Trace was hard around the outside exterior but a softy on the inside. He was strong, protective, sweet and loving. He was a force to be reckon with but would give you the shirt off his back. Even though he was damaged and scarred for life from his childhood demons, Ember was able to see past all of that and see the beauty that was deep down in Trace.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>..."You, and how my life is so different from how it would have been without you. You saw past a damaged surface and found the man beneath it. More, you loved that man and allowed him the honor of loving you."</i>
</b><br /><br /><b>
  <i>"No one ever has, or ever will, know me the way you do. You're inside me, Ember, you are my heart and you are my soul."</i>
</b><br /><br />Ember wasn't strong but she wasn't very fragile or overly weak either. The author gave Ember the perfect balance of a heroine that was very relatable and refreshing. She didn't cry over little things, freak out or run from the problems. She didn't over react or act out in naive ways either. She felt very real and very relatable to. She knew when to hold her tongue and when to let loose when she had enough. She wasn't made up of a whiny, catty, jealous, mistrusting girlfriend and she certainly didn't have a jelly spine. I loved Ember and I applaud the author for the woman she created out of her.<br /><br />This book was amazing. It had me grinning, laughing, sad, mad, and oh yeah thinking about bacon and cake-pops. I think the story line, twists and turns of the plot, the love story part of the book and over all the secondary cast of characters as well as the flow of the story were done wonderfully. I enjoyed every second of this book. I didn't want to put it down and was on the "edge of my seat" on a few things. <br /><br />The cast of secondary characters were awesome, well at least the family and friends were that is. They made you care for them, love them, laugh with them, and appreciate them. They honestly were a great support group for Trace and Ember as they had good advice, were loving, supportive, fun, protective and over all just were good people to have around. A few even made you swoon for them and made you hold out hope that they would have their own stories told in future books.<br /><br />As for the cake-pop, bacon and eggs comment.... Ember was in love with cake-pops. She ate them, talked a lot about them and dreamed about them. She even got others addicted to them. As for the bacon and eggs comment, that seemed to be the breakfast choice more often then not for the main couple. <br /><br />I felt the author left this book opened ended when it was all said and done. The couple's main story and twists are done but I felt like she left the option open to be able to add another story for a couple of her other characters. <br /><br />One thing I wished hadn't been thrown out there so much were the:<b> I LOVE YOU's</b>. I totally get why it was said a lot but at times it felt too much. Also, the ending was a tad rushed before the epilogue.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>SIDE NOTE:</i>
</b> If I start playing my kids Wii, I can only blame this book too. :oP </span>
  <a data-text-id="16077583292968981714" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer556523391" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16628775025416698454">I hope whenever I decide to write a story, and it turns into a self- published book, that I heed the words in my own reviews. Lot's of writers have stories to tell, but execution of those stories, however controlled it can be, and reader reception of them are left to luck, chemistry, and/or good editing! I am convinced. <br/><br/>It still amazes me that terribly edited books can become popular. More, when those books are let loose on the reader population with sloppy grammatical errors and plot. This is n</span>
  <span id="freeText16628775025416698454" style="display:none">I hope whenever I decide to write a story, and it turns into a self- published book, that I heed the words in my own reviews. Lot's of writers have stories to tell, but execution of those stories, however controlled it can be, and reader reception of them are left to luck, chemistry, and/or good editing! I am convinced. <br /><br />It still amazes me that terribly edited books can become popular. More, when those books are let loose on the reader population with sloppy grammatical errors and plot. This is not to say that I haven't rated some that had errors/issues, but were still gems, with 4 or 5 stars. It's just that 4 times out of 5, these books are tragic disasters.<br /><br />Beautifully Damaged is one such book. Tragically, it wanted to be a dark, romantic suspense--along the lines of Anne Stuart's<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/919357.Into_the_Fire" title="Into the Fire by Anne Stuart" rel="nofollow noopener">Into the Fire</a>or Linda Howard's<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/439941.Shades_Of_Twilight" title="Shades Of Twilight by Linda Howard" rel="nofollow noopener">Shades Of Twilight</a>---BUT, it doesn't come close because it is bogged down in overdone, new adult formula <i>virgin-heroine-meets-emotionally-fucked-with bad-boy (who is too dangerous for her)</i> and blah, blah, blah. Adding to the tragedy is that the suspense factor had merit; then the backstory and uncovering of mystery is painfully, slowly dragged out, to the point that you don't give a damn anymore. I feel like a broken record for stating this again and again in reviews, but more character depth and point of view would have helped, greatly. <br /><br />Instead, it seemed the author stumbled through telling the story in a drunken stupor, leaving out chunks of detail, jumping from one thing to another, and not "closing the deal" on what had potential to be a better story. <br /><br /> </span>
  <a data-text-id="16628775025416698454" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_510131933" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/510131933" />
    <a title="• Lisa •" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11963959-lisa"><img alt="• Lisa •" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1576172089p2/11963959.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/510131933?book_show_action=true">Jan 18, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="• Lisa •" class="user" itemprop="url" name="• Lisa •" href="/user/show/11963959-lisa">• Lisa •</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer510131933" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12526092182809714499">"I'll tell you what real love is. It is blind devotion, unquestioning self-humiliation, utter submission, trust and belief against yourself and against the whole world, giving up your whole heart and soul."<br/><br/>This started off as a bit of a slow burner.<br/>At the beginning I didn't feel like I had a great introduction or connection to the characters.<br/>The first 20% consisted of an awful best friend, a mysterious would be suitor and a female lead who needed a serious case of self discovery.<br/><br/>That being said </span>
  <span id="freeText12526092182809714499" style="display:none">"I'll tell you what real love is. It is blind devotion, unquestioning self-humiliation, utter submission, trust and belief against yourself and against the whole world, giving up your whole heart and soul."<br /><br />This started off as a bit of a slow burner.<br />At the beginning I didn't feel like I had a great introduction or connection to the characters.<br />The first 20% consisted of an awful best friend, a mysterious would be suitor and a female lead who needed a serious case of self discovery.<br /><br />That being said from that point the book turned a 180 on me and what an up, down, side to side, back and forth journey it was. This story had heartache and despair by the page full. It was almost painful to read at times.<br /><br />The main male lead - Trace, is a guarded wounded soul, a man who is drowning in his past and unable to see past it all to be loved.<br />The main female lead - Ember, a self confessed shy and sheltered woman in her early twenties is drawn to this tortured hero and is desperate to love him through his dark past, their story shows her transformation as the book progressed and I loved that loving this man ultimately was the making of her as a character.<br /><br />The story is painfully honest and by no means a light read, the author made a way of keeping secrets back and leaving the reader guessing right through the story. It is a true soul mates story one that held me as a reader at times had me captivated and frustratingly addicted - absolutely desperate for respite and a long awaited HEA.<br /><br />In short the book had a slow start, a great middle, just ok in parts and at times towards the last quarter I felt slightly bored and would skim read but it did have a lovely ending.<br /><br />Some 5 star moments but overall just a 2.5 - 3 star read for me</span>
  <a data-text-id="12526092182809714499" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  </a>
</div><div>
  <p>Source: <a href='http://theberry.com/2011/02/21/afternoon-eye-candy-random-hotties-tattooed-men-edition-29-photos/' rel='nofollow noopener'>theberry.com</a> via <a href='http://pinterest.com/karynjacobs/' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>Karen</a> on <a href='http://pinterest.com' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>Pinterest</a></p>
</div><br/><br/>The reader meets Trace Montgomery in a bar defending a rather shy Ember Walsh's honor. Right then she is warned he is a womanizing badass and to not get attached. Something about him just pulls Ember to him. Then, the chance meetings just start happening more</span>
  <span id="freeText16524093533946058727" style="display:none">This book was so, so good!! I have to admit there were some mixed reviews, but I try to start each book with an open mind. I was for sure not anywhere near disappointed.<br><br><div>
  <a href="http://pinterest.com/pin/297941331567918808/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <span>[image error]</span>
  </a>
</div><div>
  <p>Source: <a href="http://theberry.com/2011/02/21/afternoon-eye-candy-random-hotties-tattooed-men-edition-29-photos/" rel="nofollow noopener">theberry.com</a> via <a href="http://pinterest.com/karynjacobs/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Karen</a> on <a href="http://pinterest.com" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Pinterest</a></p>
</div><br><br>The reader meets Trace Montgomery in a bar defending a rather shy Ember Walsh's honor. Right then she is warned he is a womanizing badass and to not get attached. Something about him just pulls Ember to him. Then, the chance meetings just start happening more often. I guess I have a bad thing for these hot men with damaged souls. Trace Montgomery for sure is that man. I just wanted to wrap him up in a bear hug and fight his battles for him. Trace has dark secrets and doesn't let anyone in. A friendship begins and then the two start to fall for each other. <br><br>There are two parts to this book. Part one is the love story of Ember and Trace. Part two is more of a suspense story with Trace and Ember working together to figure out a murder mystery. I feel like I'm being cryptic by not giving many details away, but that's the beauty of this story finding out the details. <br><br>I did feel like in the end some of the storyline was left hanging. Maybe that means there is going to be a sequel, I need to check. I wonder what happens to evil bitch Lena and what happened with her and Todd. Also I would like to know what ended up happening to Dane. In the end it said his whole family would be brought down, but I specifically want to know what happened to Dane. Also, I have further questions about Victoria, but don't want to elaborate on that in my review due to causing spoilers. <br><br><div>
  <a href="http://pinterest.com/pin/174936766746354853/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <span>[image error]</span>
  </a>
</div><div>
  <p>Source: <a href="" rel="nofollow noopener">Uploaded by user</a> via <a href="http://pinterest.com/johnnychunga/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Johnny Chunga</a> on <a href="http://pinterest.com" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Pinterest</a></p>
</div><br><br>Overall, I really liked this book. OMG, Trace Montgomery was just straight up yummy. He was so sensitive, protective, and sweet. I loved how Ember came out of her shy shell and put Lena in her place and saved Trace in every way imaginable. Such a great read. :)<br><br></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer14268634903564287482"><b>3 stars</b><br/><br/>I don't know what about this book, I liked this book, but I did not <i>love</i> it. <br/><br/><br/>We have Ember Welsh, a 23 year old virginal girl that falls in love with a stranger named Trace Montgomery after he saves her from another man that assaulted her in a crowded bar. Then fate decides to step in, and everywhere she goes, she sees him with his hoards of women. But something inside her tells her that he is more than just what he chooses to project to the world. <br/><br/>Because of Embers supercuteness, Trace s</span>
  <span id="freeText14268634903564287482" style="display:none"><b>3 stars</b><br /><br />I don't know what about this book, I liked this book, but I did not <i>love</i> it. <br /><br /><br />We have Ember Welsh, a 23 year old virginal girl that falls in love with a stranger named Trace Montgomery after he saves her from another man that assaulted her in a crowded bar. Then fate decides to step in, and everywhere she goes, she sees him with his hoards of women. But something inside her tells her that he is more than just what he chooses to project to the world. <br /><br />Because of Embers supercuteness, Trace starts to fall for her, and after a particularly nasty incident with her best-friend's boyfriend and his friend, Trace moves her in with him in his apartment. Then she meets Rafe, Trace's best-friend who tells her that if she truly loves Trace then she should fight for him when he pushes her away. <br /><br />So Trace actually is an asshole and does push her away, but then he realizes that he cannot live without her and tells her everything about his past, which mainly constitutes of abusive father and negligent mother. And then even more secrets come out and then a happily ever after. <br /><br />Why I don't love it? <br /><br /><br /><br />Just humor me by checking out the cliches:<br /><br />1. Innocent virgin female protagonist: Check<br />2. Tormented male protagonist: Check<br />3. Boy is manwhore: Check<br />4. <b>INSTA LOVE!</b>: Check<br />5. Boy loves the innocent girl: Check<br />6. Boy saves girl: Check<br />7. Boy is a dick to girl, but girl still comes back to him after he quotes motherfucking classics to her: Check<br />8. Abusive parents: Check<br />9. Everyone loves the female protagonist, because she is the fucking <b>female protagonist</b>: Check<br />10. Innocent virginal girl is a sex goddess: Check <br />11. Boy is extremely jealous of other male competition: Check (I actually like that one, but just to be an asshole I am adding that too)<br /><br />That's a total of 11 fucking cliches and that 11 cliches too many. That was seriously all that I was doing while reading the book. Seriously people.<br /><br />The writing on the contrary, was pretty neat. I liked the flow, and the authors language was pretty humorous. All in all not a bad read, but not a great read either.</span>

<div id="review_437621718" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/437621718" />
    <a title="Vikki ~ *squee* lite ~" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3758447-vikki-squee-lite"><img alt="Vikki ~ *squee* lite ~" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1368215503p2/3758447.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/437621718?book_show_action=true">Oct 19, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Vikki ~ *squee* lite ~" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Vikki ~ *squee* lite ~" href="/user/show/3758447-vikki-squee-lite">Vikki ~ *squee* lite ~</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3758447-vikki-squee-lite?shelf=bad-boy-hero">bad-boy-hero</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3758447-vikki-squee-lite?shelf=made-me-roll-my-eyes">made-me-roll-my-eyes</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3758447-vikki-squee-lite?shelf=abuse">abuse</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3758447-vikki-squee-lite?shelf=skimed">skimed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3758447-vikki-squee-lite?shelf=books-everyone-loved-but-me">books-everyone-loved-but-me</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer437621718" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7271766562466221350">This felt like two books in one. Part one : the love story between Ember and Trace. <br/><br/> I liked Trace - he was certainly the epic bad-boy - hot, tattoos, underground fighter, tons of ladies. Ember was the quite good girl - complete with her virginity at the at of 23. <br/><br/>The story had a lot of potential, but there were a lot of things holding it back. There were odd turns of phrase (for instance the hero talks about " bedding" the heroine - a term I've never heard of from a modern day bad boy - or any </span>
  <span id="freeText7271766562466221350" style="display:none">This felt like two books in one. Part one : the love story between Ember and Trace. <br /><br /> I liked Trace - he was certainly the epic bad-boy - hot, tattoos, underground fighter, tons of ladies. Ember was the quite good girl - complete with her virginity at the at of 23. <br /><br />The story had a lot of potential, but there were a lot of things holding it back. There were odd turns of phrase (for instance the hero talks about " bedding" the heroine - a term I've never heard of from a modern day bad boy - or any modern day hero). There were issues with tenses, misuse of words (too vs to) crazy run on sentences. Frankly, I am the last person to harp on these things, and, usually I don't even notice, but the issues were enough to pull me out of the book. <br /><br />Ember was also an odd character. She was suppose to be terminally shy - but then her father (who she was suppose to be uber close to) tell her that her best friend of ten years has been undermining her confidence and keeping her in shell on purpose. Now, why would a father who loves her so much let that continue for ten years without protest. After this revelation, years of shyness suddenly gets striped away. <br /><br />Part two of the book was a murder mystery and stalker novel. This part was more interesting, although the lack of paragraphs sometimes made it hard to read. <br /><br />Overall, the book was disappointing, in large part because it has so much potential that gets lost. </span>
  <a data-text-id="7271766562466221350" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_509598544" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/509598544" />
    <a title="Sam" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7989244-sam"><img alt="Sam" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1354774536p2/7989244.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/509598544?book_show_action=true">Jan 17, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sam" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sam" href="/user/show/7989244-sam">Sam</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer509598544" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12756631266504681231">I absolutely loved this book! This is a beautiful well written love story that you will not be able to put down!<br/><br/>Ember is a sweet girl who is beautiful on the outside as well as in, Trace is a broken man who hurts himself and does things to Ember that are so wrong, yet he is doing them because he thinks that he is not good enough for her and that it's the right thing to do. The road for Ember and Trace isn’t easy by any means and there are a lot of bumps and obstacles.<br/><br/>There were so many twists an</span>
  <span id="freeText12756631266504681231" style="display:none">I absolutely loved this book! This is a beautiful well written love story that you will not be able to put down!<br /><br />Ember is a sweet girl who is beautiful on the outside as well as in, Trace is a broken man who hurts himself and does things to Ember that are so wrong, yet he is doing them because he thinks that he is not good enough for her and that it's the right thing to do. The road for Ember and Trace isn’t easy by any means and there are a lot of bumps and obstacles.<br /><br />There were so many twists and turns that your left with wanting more and you just wanted to get through to the end to find out what and how. I really liked the fact that all these revelations just made Trace and Ember’s relationship stronger.<br /><br />This was so much more than just a romance, there was suspense and mystery and I highly recommend this book to everyone, I know it is a book that I will read again and again! <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12756631266504681231" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('MTLMlwrcFcaKKLOfsON31hutCA2jwX1ZfY8jsqSn9XWuyR416AR4pfUl0VoyiOnGSDHjKGGcYf0FCZ3zvz65Lg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('zR9SEKowubqMFaip3DdFrLWUcz2k3c13SUuH52WRuHJS5ICySOjU2fMYymxeXNu85giYGGaA0dMxzTmmfgj0KQ==')})
  }
